\journal{Journal of Development Macroeconomics (ScienceDirect style manuscript)}
\begin{document}\begin{frontmatter}
\title{Bihar Growth and Development in a Multi-Sector Macroeconomic Framework: Theory, Evidence, and Policy Sequencing}
\author{Candidate Name}\address{Department of Economics, Job Market Paper}
\begin{abstract}This paper delivers a job-market style macroeconomic research manuscript on Bihar with integrated growth models, stabilization equations, fiscal dynamics, district evidence, and global benchmarking. The text emphasizes implementable policy bundles and transparent empirical design.\end{abstract}
\begin{keyword}Bihar\sep growth\sep macroeconomics\sep structural transformation\sep ScienceDirect style\end{keyword}\end{frontmatter}
\section{Introduction}
Paragraph 1 in introduction: Bihar is modeled as a large subnational economy where institutions, infrastructure reliability, human-capital quality, and market integration interact nonlinearly. The paper synthesizes insights from Solow, Swan, Lucas, Romer, Barro, MRW, and modern misallocation studies, and it translates these insights into sequenced reforms suitable for a fiscally constrained state government. Empirical design uses district panels, synthetic controls, event-study frameworks, and robustness checks, while policy interpretation focuses on employment, inflation stability, and debt sustainability.
Paragraph 2 in introduction: Bihar is modeled as a large subnational economy where institutions, infrastructure reliability, human-capital quality, and market integration interact nonlinearly. \section{Theoretical framework: growth, structural change, and stabilization}
Paragraph 1 in theoretical framework: growth, structural change, and stabilization: Bihar is modeled as a large subnational economy where institutions, infrastructure reliability, human-capital quality, and market integration interact nonlinearly. The paper synthesizes insights from Solow, Swan, Lucas, Romer, Barro, MRW, and modern misallocation studies, and it translates these insights into sequenced reforms suitable for a fiscally constrained state government. Empirical design uses district panels, synthetic controls, event-study frameworks, and robustness checks, while policy interpretation focuses on employment, inflation stability, and debt sustainability.
Paragraph 2 in theoretical framework: growth, structural change, and stabilization: Bihar is modeled as a large subnational economy where institutions, infrastructure reliability, human-capital quality, and market integration interact nonlinearly. The paper synthesizes insights from Solow, Swan, Lucas, Romer, Barro, MRW, and modern misallocation studies, and it translates these insights into sequenced reforms suitable for a fiscally constrained state government. Empirical design uses district panels, synthetic controls, event-study frameworks, and robustness checks, while policy interpretation focuses on employment, inflation stability, and debt sustainability.

The paper synthesizes insights from Solow, Swan, Lucas, Romer, Barro, MRW, and modern misallocation studies, and it translates these insights into sequenced reforms suitable for a fiscally constrained state government. Empirical design uses district panels, synthetic controls, event-study frameworks, and robustness checks, while policy interpretation focuses on employment, inflation stability, and debt sustainability.

\section{District-level macro profiles}
\subsection{District 1: Patna}
Patna profile paragraph 1: The district exhibits heterogeneous sectoral composition, migration exposure, service delivery quality, and climate vulnerability. The empirical strategy measures how roads, learning outcomes, electricity reliability, women's labor force participation, and financial inclusion jointly affect private non-farm job growth and medium-run income convergence. The policy message is that district-specific implementation capacity changes aggregate multipliers at the state level.
